4-160: Penalty
ARTICLE A.
GENERAL PROVISIONS
4-101: DEFINITIONS:
   The following words and phrases when used in this chapter shall have the
meanings prescribed in this section except in those cases where the context
clearly indicates a different meaning:
ANIMAL: Any horse, mule, donkey, pony, cow, sheep, goat, hog, dog, cat, rabbit,
chicken, goose, duck, turkey, or other animal or fowl.
AT LARGE:
   A.   Not securely confined by a fence or other means on premises under the
control of, or occupied by, the owner; or
   B.    Not under the control of the owner, a member of his immediate family
over twelve (12) years of age or an agent of the owner, by leash, whether on
the owner's premises or not.
OWNER: Any person, firm or entity owning, harboring or keeping an animal. The
occupant of any premises on which a domesticated or tamed animal remains, or to
which it customarily returns for a period of ten (10) days or more, shall be
deemed to be harboring or keeping the animal.
VICIOUS DOG: A dog which has bitten, or attempted to bite, any person or other
animal without provocation, or which attacks, or barks or growls at and acts as
if it intends to attack or bite, or bites a person or persons, when not unduly
provoked.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-102: ANIMALS NOT TO BE AT LARGE:
   No owner shall permit any animal, including fowl, owned, harbored or kept by
him to be at large within the town. It is unlawful for any animal as provided
in this section to be at large at any time within the town of Dickson.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-103: TURNING OUT ANIMALS AT LARGE UNLAWFUL:
   It is unlawful for any person to open any enclosure in which any animal is
confined as required by this chapter so as to turn the animal at large, or in
any manner to turn the animal out to enable it to be at large.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-104: PASTURING IN PUBLIC AREAS ILLEGAL:
   It is unlawful for any person to stake, confine or pasture any animal on any
public school ground or other public property, federal, state, town or other,
on any railroad right of way, or on any property without the consent of the
person owning or controlling such property.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-105: ANIMALS WHICH DISTURB PROHIBITED:
   It is unlawful for any person to keep or harbor within the town of Dickson
any dog or other animal who by barking, howling or otherwise, disturbs the
peace and quiet of any person. The keeping of such an animal is hereby declared
to be a nuisance.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-106: BUILDINGS FOR ANIMALS; LOCATION:
   A.   Every building wherein any horse, mule, donkey, pony, cow, goat, sheep
or animal raised for furbearing purposes that is kept within the town of
Dickson, shall be constructed of such material and in such manner that it can
be kept clean and sanitary at all times.
   B.   Every such building, if located within two hundred feet (200') of any
apartment house, hotel, motel, restaurant, boarding house, retail food store,
building used for educational, religious or hospital purposes or residence
other than that occupied by the owner or occupant of the premises upon which
such animal is kept, shall be provided with a watertight and flytight
receptacle for manure, of such size as to hold all accumulations of manure.
Such receptacle shall be emptied sufficiently often and in such manner as to
prevent it from being or becoming a nuisance, and shall be kept covered at all
times except when open during the deposit or removal of manure or refuse. No
manure shall be allowed to accumulate on such premises except in such
receptacle.
   C.   No building, place or establishment wherein animals are kept, shall be
maintained closer than forty feet (40') from any apartment house, hotel, motel,
restaurant, boarding house, retail food store, building used for educational,
religious or hospital purposes or residence other than that occupied by the
owner or occupant of the premises upon which such animal is kept.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-107: MANURE:
   Manure shall be hauled outside the town of Dickson in a manner which does
not jeopardize the public health, or else shall be spread evenly upon the
ground and turned under at once or as soon as the weather permits.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-108: REQUIREMENT OF CLEANLINESS OF BUILDINGS:
   Every place or building wherein an animal is kept or permitted to be kept
shall be maintained in a clean and sanitary condition at all times, devoid of
rodents and vermin and free from objectionable odors.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-109: ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER OR POLICE OFFICER TO INSPECT:
   A health or animal control officer or peace officer, upon complaint of any
person, shall inspect any structure or place where an animal is kept, and may
do so on his own initiative after notification of his intent to do so to the
chairman of the board of trustees or a member of the board of trustees of the
town of Dickson in the chairman's absence. He may issue any such reasonable
order as he may deem necessary to the owner of the animal to cause the animal
to be kept as provided in this chapter or in a manner so as not to constitute a
nuisance. He may make a complaint before the Dickson municipal judge against
any person for violation of any provision of this chapter or of any such
reasonable order, but this procedure shall not be construed to abridge the
right of others to make such complaints.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
ARTICLE B.
DOG AND CAT VACCINATION AND HEALTH
4-120: DOGS AND CATS TO BE VACCINATED:
   The owner or keeper of any dog or cat of six (6) months of age or older
within the town limits of Dickson shall have the dog or cat vaccinated against
rabies by a licensed veterinarian every calendar year, before May 1 thereof.
Owners shall affix, or have affixed, to the collar or harness of each
vaccinated dog or cat a metal disc with sufficient information thereon that the
vaccination certificate covering the animal may be readily traced.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-121: VICIOUS DOG MAY BE KILLED:
   Any person may kill a dog in self-defense or in defense of another when the
dog, without undue provocation, bites him or the other, or attacks, or attempts
to bite or attack him or the other in such manner that an ordinarily prudent
person would be led to believe that the person toward whom the efforts of the
dog are directed is about to be bitten or otherwise physically harmed.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-122: DOGS MUZZLED AND CATS CONFINED:
   A.   When a health officer or peace officer determines and certifies that a
dog, cat or other animal in the town or within five (5) miles of the town of
Dickson is or was infected with rabies and that an epidemic of rabies threatens
the town, the board of trustees of Dickson, by resolution, may order all dogs
to be muzzled when at large within the town of Dickson, and if deemed
desirable, all cats to be confined, during a period of time to be determined by
the board of trustees. Such resolution or an adequate notice of its passage
shall be published in a newspaper of general circulation within the town and
shall go into effect on the date following such publication unless the
resolution prescribes a later time.
   B.   While such resolution is in effect, it is unlawful for any owner to
permit an unmuzzled dog or cat to be at large in violation of such resolution,
or for any such dog or cat to be at large in violation thereof.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-123: RABIES CONTROL AND PROCEDURES:
   A.   Every animal that bites or scratches a person shall be reported within
four (4) hours from the time of the incident to a peace officer, a member of
the board of trustees of Dickson, or an animal control officer, and said animal
shall thereupon be securely quarantined at an approved animal control shelter
or veterinary clinic within Carter County, Oklahoma, at the owner's expense,
for a period of ten (10) days. The animal shall not be released from quarantine
except by permission and approval of a licensed veterinarian or an animal
control officer familiar with the incident, along with at least one member of
the board of trustees. Failure of the owner to promptly quarantine the affected
animal shall cause said owner to be deemed guilty of an offense.
   B.   In the case of stray animals, or in the case of animals whose ownership
is not known, such quarantine shall be at an animal shelter or veterinary
facility, at the town's expense.
   C.   The owner, upon demand by an employee empowered to enforce this
chapter, shall forthwith surrender any animal that has bitten or scratched a
human being, or which if suspected of having been exposed to rabies, for
supervised quarantine, the expense for which shall be borne by the owner and
the animal may be reclaimed by the owner if adjudged free of rabies.
   D.   When an animal under quarantine has been diagnosed as being rabid, or
suspected by a licensed veterinarian as being rabid, and dies while under such
observation, the animal control officer or veterinarian shall immediately send
the head of such animal to the state health department for pathological
examination, and shall notify the proper public health officer of reports of
human contacts and diagnosis made of the suspected animal.
   E.   When one or both reports give a positive diagnosis of rabies, a health
officer for the town may recommend a townside quarantine for a period of up to
six (6) months, and upon the invoking of such quarantine, no animal shall be
taken into the streets or town proper of Dickson during such period of
quarantine. During such quarantine period, no animal shall be taken or shipped
from the town of Dickson without written permission of quarantine invoking
health officer for the town.
   F.   During such period of rabies quarantine as herein designated, every
animal bitten by an animal adjudged to be rabid shall be treated for such
rabies infection by a licensed veterinarian or held under six (6) months
quarantine by the owner in the same manner as other animals are quarantined.
   G.   In event there are additional positive cases of rabies occurring during
the period of the quarantine, such period of quarantine may be extended for an
additional six (6) month period.
   H.   While in quarantine, no person shall kill or cause to be killed any
rabid animal, any animal suspected of having been exposed to rabies, or any
animal biting or scratching a human being, except as herein provided, nor to
remove same from the town limits of Dickson without written permission from the
health officer of the town or an animal control officer, or a member of the
board of trustees.
   I.   The carcass of any dead animal exposed to rabies shall upon demand be
surrendered to the animal control officer, or a demanding peace officer.
   J.   The animal control officer or veterinarian shall direct the disposition
of any animal found to be infected with rabies.
   K.   No person shall fail or refuse to surrender any animal for quarantine
as required herein when demand is made therefor by an employee empowered to
enforce this chapter. Such refusal shall be deemed to be an offense.
   L.   It is the duty of every physician, veterinarian or other practitioner
to report to the animal control officer of Dickson, or the board of trustees of
said municipality, the names and addresses of persons treated for bites
inflicted by animals, together with such other information as will be helpful
in rabies control.
   M.   It is the duty of every licensed veterinarian to report to the Dickson
animal control officer, a peace officer, and/or a member of the board of
trustees of Dickson, his diagnosis of any animal observed by him to be a rabid
suspect from the Dickson town limits and a surrounding area of five (5) miles.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
ARTICLE C.
ANIMAL SHELTER
4-130: ANIMAL SHELTER ESTABLISHED:
   The town of Dickson may establish an animal shelter when fiscally practical.
The board of trustees of Dickson may further contract with another governmental
agency for the use of an animal shelter.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-131: ANIMALS TO BE IMPOUNDED, ENTRY ON PROPERTY:
   The animal control officer, a peace officer, or such other officer or
employee of the town of Dickson, Oklahoma, as the board of trustees may
authorize shall take into custody and impound any animal found at large or in
violation of any provisions of the ordinances of the town. In taking an animal
into custody under authority of this article, the animal control officer or
other officer or employee of the town may enter into private property to gain
custody of the animal.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-132: IMPOUNDMENT, DESCRIPTION, NOTICE, DISPOSITION:
   A.   The animal control officer or authorized peace officer or employee of
the town of Dickson shall leave with the town clerk a complete registry of the
animal taken to an approved animal shelter. Information posted shall include
the species, breed, color, sex, license number if available, date of
impoundment, and name, address and phone number of the owner if known.
   B.   Not later than forty eight (48) hours after impounding the animal, the
town clerk shall call the owner, if known, or mail notice at the address shown
on town records, if any, to notify them of the provisions of this chapter.
   C.   All impounded animals, unless a rabies suspect, shall be maintained for
at least seventy two (72) hours at an approved shelter. After all reasonable
attempts for reuniting the animal with its owner have been made during the
seventy two (72) hours, the animal can then be placed with an animal adoption
agency or an animal pound.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-133: BREAKING OR ENTERING POUND:
   A.   No unauthorized person shall:
      1.   Break or attempt to break open an animal pound, or take or let out
any animal therefrom;
      2.   Take or attempt to take from any officer or employee of the town of
Dickson any animal taken into custody as provided by this chapter; or
      3.   In any manner interfere with or hinder an officer or employee in the
discharge of his duties relating to the taking into custody and impounding of
animals as provided in this chapter.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-134: FEES FOR IMPOUNDING:
   A.   The town board of trustees, by motion or resolution shall determine the
fees to be charged for impounding and keeping animals.
   B.   Any person redeeming an impounded animal shall pay the required fees to
the town clerk and present his receipt therefor to the person in charge of the
pound before the latter releases the animal.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-135: RECLAMATION OF IMPOUNDED ANIMALS:
   Reclamation of impounded animals may be made as provided in this section.
The party desiring to reclaim an animal shall present to the animal control
officer or other employee, who may be designated by the town board of trustees
proof of ownership, and proof that any dog or cat is currently vaccinated for
rabies or return proof of vaccination within three (3) days after the date the
animal is released. The party desiring to reclaim any animal shall pay the
applicable pound fee and show evidence to the animal control officer that the
fee has been paid. The animal control officer shall thereupon release the
reclaimed animal to the party. Any party violating any provision of this
section or failing to return proof of vaccination as provided herein shall,
upon conviction, be punished by a fine and taxing of court costs, in the
discretion of the Dickson municipal court.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-136: DISPOSITION AND SALE OF IMPOUNDED ANIMALS:
   A.   At the end of the period prescribed in this article, animals that have
not been redeemed by the owner thereof shall be destroyed in a humane manner or
sold in the manner hereinafter provided. Further, the animal may be adopted by
any citizen of the town upon payment of the applicable pound and license fees
for said animal. The board of trustees deems it to be their policy that
impounded animals shall first be offered for adoption, with provision that any
prospective adopting person may petition the board of trustees for a payment
plan, to allow said person to pay the impound fees and license costs.
   B.   The sales herein provided for shall be conducted by the person in
charge of the animal shelter as may be designated by the board of trustees.
Such sales shall be for cash to the highest bidder, but the animals shall not
be sold in any event for less than that sum required to cover the impounding
fee, board bill, vaccination expense, and license fees where applicable. If
there is no bid, or an insufficient amount is bid as herein provided, the
person in charge of the pound shall destroy such animal, unless he believes it
to be for the best interests of the town to retain the animal and offer it for
sale at a later date. The proceeds of the sale, less the vaccination fees which
shall be paid to the person administering the vaccination, shall be forthwith
delivered to the town clerk.
   C.   The purchaser of an animal at a sale held as provided herein, shall
acquire absolute title to the animal purchased.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
ARTICLE D.
CRUELTY TO ANIMALS
4-140: ANIMAL CRUELTY PROHIBITED:
   It is unlawful for any person to wilfully, maliciously or knowingly treat an
animal, bird or fowl in a cruel or inhumane manner; or to knowingly neglect an
animal, bird or fowl belonging to him or in his custody in a cruel or inhumane
manner.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-141: POISONING ANIMALS:
   It is unlawful for a person to wilfully poison any dog or other animal, or
knowingly expose poison so that the same may be taken by such an animal.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
4-142: ENCOURAGING ANIMALS TO FIGHT:
   It is unlawful for any person to instigate or encourage a fight between
animals or to encourage one animal to attack, pursue or annoy another animal.
It is further unlawful for any person to keep a house, building, structure,
pit, or other place used for fights between animals.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
ARTICLE E.
KENNELS
4-150: KENNELS, LICENSING:
   A.   Any person owning, possessing, keeping or harboring for the purpose of
breeding, selling or boarding, more than three (3) dogs or cats six (6) months
old or older shall be deemed to be operating a private kennel. No person shall
operate a private kennel without first obtaining an annual permit to operate
the kennel from the town clerk. (Ord. 80, 3-26-2012)
   B.   Permits under this section shall permit the animal control officer to
inspect the premises used as a private kennel. Private kennels shall be
maintained in accordance with written standards of the American Humane Society
and applicable federal and state laws and regulations.
   C.   Any person applying for a kennel permit from the town of Dickson shall
first prove to the board of trustees that timely notice has been given to any
person who resides or owns lands within one thousand five hundred feet (1,500')
of the proposed site of the kennel of the date, time, and place of hearing the
application, which shall be furnished by the town clerk. The notice shall
include the date, time and place of the hearing of the kennel application
before the board and shall be given no less than fifteen (15) days prior to the
date of the hearing. The notice shall be given to neighbors and landowners
within one thousand five hundred feet (1,500') of the proposed kennel site by
registered mail, personal delivery if available, and by publication of at least
one legal notice in a newspaper of general circulation in Carter County,
Oklahoma. Applications for kennel permits shall be available from the Dickson
town clerk. Before hearing the application, the board of trustees must first be
satisfied that diligent effort has been employed to notify all affected persons
of the application. (Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
   D.   The annual fee for kennel permits shall be one hundred dollars
($100.00). (Ord. 80, 3-26-2012)
ARTICLE F.
PENALTIES
4-160: PENALTY:
   Any person, firm, entity, or corporation who violates any ordinance or
provision of this chapter, or who violates or refuses or neglects to carry out
any reasonable order made by the animal control officer, a peace officer
employed by the town of Dickson, or a designated member of the board of
trustees, shall upon conviction thereof, be punished as provided by this code.
(Ord. 48, 3-19-1998)
CHAPTER 2
DANGEROUS DOGS
SECTION:
4-200: Definitions
4-201: Certificates Of Registration For Certain Dogs Required; Exemptions; Fee
4-202: Muzzles And Restraint Of Certain Dogs
4-203: Dogs Not To Be Declared Dangerous
4-204: Confiscation Of A Dangerous Dog
4-205: Fines
4-206: Purpose
4-207: Penalty
4-200: DEFINITIONS:
ANIMAL WELFARE: A local government authority acting alone or in concert with
other local governmental units for enforcement of the animal welfare laws of
the town, county, state, the shelter and welfare of animals.
ANIMAL WELFARE OFFICER: Any individual employed, contracted with, or appointed
by animal welfare for the purpose of aiding the enforcement of any law or
ordinance relating to the licensure of animals, control of animals, or seizure
and impoundment of animals, and includes any state or local enforcement officer
or other employee whose duties in whole or in part include assignments that
involve the seizure and impoundment of any animal. The words animal welfare
officer shall include certified law enforcement officer, reserve officer, or
full time employee employed by the town of Dickson.
DANGEROUS DOG: Any dog that:
   A.   Has inflicted severe injury on a human being without provocation on
public or private property, or
   B.   Has been previously found to be potentially dangerous, the owner having
received notice of such by the animal authority in writing and the dog
thereafter aggressively bites, attacks, or endangers the safety of humans.
OWNER: Any person, firm, corporation, organization or department possessing,
harboring, keeping, having an interest in, or having control or custody of an
animal.
POTENTIALLY DANGEROUS DOGS: Any dog that when unprovoked inflicts bites on
humans either on public or private property.
PROPER ENCLOSURE OF A DANGEROUS DOG: While on the owner's property a dangerous
dog shall be securely confined indoors, or in a securely enclosed and locked
pen or structure with at least one hundred fifty (150) square feet of space for
each dog kept there in which is over six (6) months of age, and which is
suitable to prevent the entry of children and designed to prevent the animal
from escaping. Such pen or structure shall have secure top, and shall also
provide protection from the elements for the dog.
SEVERE INJURY: Any physical injury that results in broken bones or lacerations,
requiring sutures, or cosmetic surgery.
(Ord. 79, 9-26-2011)
4-201: CERTIFICATES OF REGISTRATION FOR CERTAIN DOGS REQUIRED; EXEMPTIONS; FEE:
   A.   Certificate Of Registration For Certain Dogs Required: It is unlawful
for an owner to have a dangerous dog without certificate of registration issued
according to this chapter. This chapter shall not apply to dogs used by law
enforcement officials. (Ord. 79, 9-26-2011)
   B.   Exemptions: A certificate of registration shall be issued to the owner
of such animal if the owner presents to the animal control unit sufficient
evidence of: (Ord. 80, 3-26-2012)
      1.   A proper enclosure to confine a dangerous dog and the posting of the
premises with a clearly visible warning sign that there is a dangerous dog on
the property. In addition, the owner shall conspicuously display a sign with a
warning symbol that informs children of the presence of a dangerous dog; and
      2.   A policy of liability insurance, such as homeowners' insurance, or
surety bond used by an insurer qualified under title 36 of the Oklahoma state
statutes in the amount of not less than fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00)
insuring the owner for any personal injuries inflicted by the dangerous animal.
   C.   Fee: A fee of ten dollars ($10.00) shall be remitted to the director of
finance for the certificate of registration.
(Ord. 79, 9-26-2011)
4-202: MUZZLES AND RESTRAINT OF CERTAIN DOGS:
   It is unlawful for an owner of a dangerous dog to permit the dog to be
outside the proper enclosure unless the dog is muzzled and restrained by a
substantial chain or leash and under physical restraining of a responsible
person over sixteen (16) years of age. The muzzle shall be made in a manner
that will not cause injury to the dog or interfere with its vision or
respiration but shall prevent it from biting any person or animal.
(Ord. 79, 9-26-2011)
4-203: DOGS NOT TO BE DECLARED DANGEROUS:
   Dogs shall not be declared dangerous if the threat, injury or damage was
sustained by a person who, at the time, was committing a wilful trespass or
other tort upon the premises occupied by the owner of the dog, or was
tormenting, abusing, or assaulting the dog or has, in the past, been observed
or reported to have tormented, abused, or assaulted the dog or was committing
or attempting to commit a crime.
(Ord. 79, 9-26-2011)
4-204: CONFISCATION OF A DANGEROUS DOG:
   Any dangerous dog shall be immediately confiscated by the chief of police or
law enforcement officer if: (Ord. 80, 3-26-2012)
   A.   The dog is not validly registered according to this chapter;
   B.   The owner does not secure the liability insurance coverage or surety
bond required by this chapter;
   C.   The dog is not maintained in the proper enclosure; and
   D.   The dog is outside of the dwelling of the owner or outside the proper
enclosure and not under the physical restraint of the responsible person. (Ord.
79, 9-26-2011)
   Any dangerous dog confiscated pursuant to this section and not reclaimed by
its owner under the requirements of this chapter within thirty (30) days from
the date of notice of confiscation shall be deemed abandoned and will be
euthanized. (Ord. 80, 3-26-2012)
4-205: FINES:
   Any fine imposed as a result of a violation of this chapter, at the
discretion of the court, may be offset by payments made by the dog owner to any
victim of an attack by the dog. However, insurance payments may not be
considered as an offset. (Ord. 79, 9-26-2011)
4-206: PURPOSE:
   It is the purpose of this chapter to provide additional and cumulative
remedies to control dangerous and potentially dangerous dogs. Nothing in this
chapter shall be construed to abridge or alter rights of action or remedies of
victims under the common law or statutory law, criminal or civil. (Ord. 79, 9-
26-2011)
4-207: PENALTY:
   Violation of this chapter shall result in a penalty of five (5) days in jail
or not more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) plus any costs or destruction of
dog. (Ord. 79, 9-26-2011)
PART 5
BUILDING REGULATIONS AND CODES
CHAPTER 1
BUILDING CODES AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
5-101: Codes Adopted
5-102: Fire Limits
5-103: Violations; Penalties
5-104: Mobile Home Requirements
5-101: CODES ADOPTED:
   The most recent editions of the following international codes relating to
building, plumbing, electrical installations, and fire prevention, recommended
by the International Code Council, Inc., are hereby adopted by reference, as
provided by 11 Oklahoma Statutes section 14-107; 47 Oklahoma Statutes section
582:
   International building code;
   International plumbing code;
   International mechanical code;
   National electrical code;
   International fire code.
   Copies of said codes, rules and standards shall be kept in the office of the
town clerk for use, inspection and examination by the public.
(Ord. 77, 4-26-2010)
5-102: FIRE LIMITS:
   A.   Defined: The fire limits zone of the town shall be defined as the town
limits.
   B.   Buildings Within Fire Limits: No building or structure, other than
residential housing, shall be built, constructed, improved or added to that
situated within the zone known as fire limit zone unless said structure, in
addition to the building, plumbing, mechanical, and electrical code
requirements adopted in section
5-101 of this chapter, also meets the plans and specifications of the Oklahoma
state fire marshal for business and/or public buildings, which plans and
specifications by the state fire marshal are hereby adopted by reference
thereto.
(Ord. 77, 4-26-2010)
5-103: VIOLATIONS; PENALTIES:
   A.   Penalties:
      1.   Any person who violates any provision of this chapter pertaining to
building, plumbing and electrical codes or fails to comply with any of the
requirements thereof or who shall install electrical services, plumbing and/or
mechanical works, or construct or erect buildings or additions thereto in
violation of an approved plan or directive of the town mayor, or does work
without licenses required under the provisions of this chapter shall be guilty
of an offense, which shall be punishable as provided in section 1-108 of this
code.
      2.   Any person, firm, or corporation who engages in any business, trade,
or vocation for which a license, permit, certificate, or certificate of
registration is required by this chapter without having first obtained a valid
license, permit, certificate or certificate of registration as required, or who
shall fail to do anything required by this chapter or by any code adopted
herein, or who shall violate any lawful regulations as provided in this chapter
shall be guilty of an offense and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable
as provided in section 1-108 of this code.
   B.   Injunctive Relief: No penalty imposed by and pursuant to this section
shall interfere with the right of the town to make application to a court of
proper jurisdiction for injunctive relief or other appropriate action, legal or
equitable, against such person, firm, or corporation deemed to be violating the
building, plumbing, mechanical, and electrical codes as set forth in this
chapter.
   C.   Application To Corporations And Associations: The violation of any
terms or provisions of this chapter by any corporation or association shall
subject the principal officers and agents thereof, actively in charge of the
business and of such corporation or association, to the penalties provided
herein.
(Ord. 77, 4-26-2010)
5-104: MOBILE HOME REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   The most recent Oklahoma manufactured home installation standards
relating to installation of a mobile home, are hereby adopted by reference, as
provided by Oklahoma law: 47 Oklahoma Statutes section 582, establishment of
the Oklahoma used motor vehicle and parts commission.
   B.   The commission shall promulgate rules for licensing of manufactured
home installers and the installation, which is blocking, anchoring and leveling
of mobile and manufactured homes that meet the standards of the manufacturer's
manual or the commission. Copy of said law shall be kept for reference in the
office of the town clerk for use, inspection and examination by the public.
(Ord. 77, 4-26-2010)
PART 6
COURT
CHAPTER 1
MUNICIPAL COURT
SECTION:
6-101: Definitions
6-102: Established
6-103: Jurisdiction
6-104: Judge; Appointment, Duties
6-105: Appeal Of Conviction; Notice
6-106: Prosecuting Attorney Designated
6-107: Court Clerk; Appointment, Duties
6-108: Compensation Of Court Officials
6-109: Fines And Costs
6-110: Appointment Of Attorney In Judge's Absence
6-111: New Court Provisions Effective
6-112: Rules Of Court
6-113: Enforcement
6-114: Collection Fee
6-101: DEFINITIONS:
 
BOARD OF TRUSTEES OR BOARD:         The mayor and board of trustees of the town
                                    of Dickson, Oklahoma.
MUNICIPAL COURT:                    The municipal court of the town of Dickson,
                                    Oklahoma.
MUNICIPAL COURT CLERK:              The appointed clerk of the municipal court
                                    of the town of Dickson, Oklahoma.
MUNICIPAL JUDGE OF MUNICIPAL COURT: The appointed municipal judge of the town
                                    of Dickson, Oklahoma.
 
(Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-102: ESTABLISHED:
   A municipal court is hereby established in the town of Dickson, Oklahoma, a
municipal governmental corporation operating under the statutory town form of
government. Said municipal court shall be referred to as the municipal court of
the town of Dickson, Oklahoma. (Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-103: JURISDICTION:
   The municipal court of the town of Dickson, Oklahoma, shall have all of the
powers, authority, and jurisdiction granted a municipal court in a municipality
operating under the statutory form of government (board of trustees) by
Oklahoma Statutes or common law. Any amendments or modifications of a municipal
government's municipal court implemented by the Oklahoma legislature,
applicable to statutory towns, subsequent to the adoption of this chapter,
including, but not limited to, increases in municipal court's jurisdictions and
authority to levy monetary fines and assessments, as well as to tax court
costs, shall automatically inure to the benefit of the town of Dickson,
Oklahoma, and its municipal court shall be deemed to have acquired any
additional powers, authority and/or jurisdiction granted statutory towns by the
Oklahoma legislature at any time in the future, without further amendment of
this chapter by the board of trustees.
(Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-104: JUDGE; APPOINTMENT, DUTIES:
   There shall be a municipal judge for the town of Dickson, Oklahoma. Said
judge shall be appointed by a majority of the board of trustees of the town of
Dickson, Oklahoma, and shall serve at the board's pleasure. The municipal judge
shall at all times be an attorney licensed to practice law before the supreme
court of Oklahoma, and shall be a resident of the state of Oklahoma during his
or her tenure. The municipal judge shall discharge his or her duties
faithfully, impartially, and fairly, and shall be responsible for determining
violations of municipal ordinances of the town of Dickson, Oklahoma, and
determining appropriate penalties thereof. The municipal judge may be removed
from office at anytime by a majority vote of the board of trustees, with or
without cause.
(Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-105: APPEAL OF CONVICTION; NOTICE:
   Appeals from a conviction in the municipal court of the town of Dickson,
Oklahoma, shall be de novo to the district court of Carter County, Oklahoma, as
provided by Oklahoma law. Notice of appeal shall be filed, in writing, with the
clerk of the municipal court of Dickson and the court clerk of Carter County
within ten (10) days from date of imposition of judgment and sentence. Upon
timely filing of an appeal, the municipal judge shall certify the appeal or
supersede bond, which shall be deposited with the town municipal court clerk
and the official record or transcript. Upon notification of appeal, the clerk
of the municipal court shall promptly notify the Carter County court clerk of
the appeal and posting of bond, in conformity with state statutes. Failure to
file the notice of intent to appeal within the time frame outlined shall deem
the judgment and sentence of the municipal judge of Dickson to be final. No
extension of the time frame to file the notice of intent to appeal shall be
granted in any instance.
(Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-106: PROSECUTING ATTORNEY DESIGNATED:
   The town attorney of Dickson shall be the designated prosecuting attorney in
the municipal court of Dickson, and shall represent the municipality on any
appeal to the district court of Carter County, Oklahoma.
(Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-107: COURT CLERK; APPOINTMENT, DUTIES:
   There shall be a municipal court clerk. Said clerk shall be appointed by the
board of trustees, and shall serve at the board's pleasure. The clerk shall be
responsible for the preparation of dockets for the municipal judge, collection
and proper deposit of fines and bonds of offenders or persons who have been
cited for violations of municipal ordinances, and shall keep an appropriate
journal thereof. The clerk shall attend all sessions of the municipal court of
Dickson, and shall be charged with the responsibility of maintaining the books,
records and dockets of the municipal court, as directed by the board of
trustees. The clerk shall also be responsible for appropriate notification to
the court clerk of Carter County, Oklahoma, of perfected appeals from the
municipal court of Dickson. The clerk shall further be responsible for prompt
reporting of all bond forfeitures, convictions and failure to pay fines or
costs, including insufficient checks, to the department of public safety of the
state of Oklahoma, or the state licensing the offender. The clerk shall further
be responsible for the proper recordation of the judgments and sentences of the
municipal judge. (Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
   The municipal court clerk shall be also designated as the deputy town clerk
and have powers and duties as the town clerk when the town clerk is
unavailable.
(Ord. 69, 12-17-2007)
6-108: COMPENSATION OF COURT OFFICIALS:
   The board of trustees shall set the compensation of the municipal judge and
municipal clerk of the town of Dickson, Oklahoma, for their duties as defined
herein.
(Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-109: FINES AND COSTS:
   The board of trustees shall implement, by separate ordinance or resolution,
appropriate fines and costs to be assessed by the municipal judge of the town
of Dickson, Oklahoma, for convictions of violations of municipal ordinances,
and shall periodically update said fines and costs in its discretion. The
schedule of fines and costs shall be limited to amounts allowed by Oklahoma
law, and shall be available at all times for public inspection.
(Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-110: APPOINTMENT OF ATTORNEY IN JUDGE'S ABSENCE:
   In event of recusal or disqualification by the municipal judge of the town
of Dickson, Oklahoma, in any case or issue, then and in said event, the board
of trustees shall appoint a licensed attorney on an interim basis, with
specific authority to hear and adjudicate specific cases or issues. The board
of trustees in such instance shall fix the compensation of the assigned
temporary judge, who shall be paid by the town clerk-treasurer.
(Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-111: NEW COURT PROVISIONS EFFECTIVE:
   The municipal court of the town of Dickson, Oklahoma, shall become effective
and shall acquire subject matter jurisdiction under this chapter and enabling
Oklahoma Statutes on August 22, 1997.
(Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-112: RULES OF COURT:
   A.   Prescribed By Judge: The municipal judge of the town of Dickson shall
have the authority to implement court rules, consistent with the laws of the
state and with the ordinances of the town, for the administration of justice
and procedure in the municipal court.
   B.   Posted: Said court rules shall be posted prominently in the town hall
of Dickson, Oklahoma, and shall govern procedures in the municipal court of the
town of Dickson, Oklahoma.
   C.   Enforcement: Obedience to the orders, rules and judgments made by the
judge or by the court may be enforced by the judge, who may fine or imprison
for contempt committed as to him while holding court, or committed against
process issued by him, in the same manner and to the same extent as the
district courts of the state of Oklahoma.
(Ord. 73, 8-24-2009)
6-113: ENFORCEMENT:
   Enforcement of ordinances of the town of Dickson, Oklahoma, shall be carried
out and performed by any law enforcement officer, including, but not limited
to, the Carter County sheriff's department, Oklahoma highway patrol, or any
other law enforcement agency operating within the corporate limits of the town
of Dickson, Oklahoma. (Ord. 44, 8-22-1997)
6-114: COLLECTION FEE 1 :
   A.   Defendant To Pay Cost: A collection fee of thirty-five percent (35%) of
Court penalties, cost fines, and fees in cases in which the accused has failed
to appear or otherwise failed to satisfy a monetary obligation imposed by the
Court, shall be added to any such case which is referred to a collection agency
for collection.
(Ord. 98, 9-26-2022)
 
Notes
1 1. 11 O.S. §22-138
PART 7
FINANCE AND TAXATION
CHAPTER 1
FINANCE AND BUDGET ADMINISTRATION
SECTION:
7-101: Depositories designated; funds to be deposited.
7-102: Funds secured by Unit Collateral System.
7-103: Purchases, how made.
7-104: When prior approval by the town board of trustees is required.
7-101: DEPOSITORIES DESIGNATED; FUNDS TO BE DEPOSITED.
   All banks and all savings and loan associations which may be so designated
by the town board of trustees shall be depositories for the funds of the town.
The town treasurer shall deposit daily all public funds received by him in such
banks or savings and loan associations.
State Law Reference: Deposits by treasurers, designation of depositories; 11
O.S. Section 12-110.
7-102: FUNDS SECURED BY UNIT COLLATERAL SYSTEM.
   The deposits of the town shall be secured by the Unit Collateral System
provided by the Oklahoma Statutes.
State Law Reference: Unit Collateral System, 62 O.S. Sections 516.1 et seq.
7-103: PURCHASES, HOW MADE.
   All purchases of supplies, materials, equipment and contractual services for
the offices, departments and agencies of the town government, shall be made by
the town board of trustees or by other town personnel in accordance with
purchase authorizations issued by the town board of trustees.
7-104: WHEN PRIOR APPROVAL BY THE TOWN BOARD OF TRUSTEES IS REQUIRED.
   Every contract for, or purchase of, supplies, materials, equipment or
contractual services for more than Seven Hundred Fifty Dollars ($750.00) shall
require the prior approval of the town board of trustees.
State Law Reference: Purchase Order Act, 62 O.S.Sections 310.1 et seq.
CHAPTER 2
SALES TAX
