10-417: BEING ABOUT PLACE WHERE GAMBLING IS GOING ON:
   It is unlawful for any person to be about in the immediate vicinity where a
person or persons are gambling, whether by playing games, operating a slot
machine or other device, or otherwise.
(1987 Code)
10-418: HARMFUL DECEPTION:
   It is unlawful for any person knowingly to deceive another, whether by
impersonation, misrepresentation, or otherwise, when such deception results in
or contributes to the loss, damage, harm or injury of the person deceived or of
a third party, or results in or contributes to the benefit of the deceiver.
(1987 Code)
10-419: FALSE OR BOGUS CHECKS:
   It is unlawful for any person, with intent to cheat and defraud, to obtain
or attempt to obtain from any person, firm or corporation, any money, property
or valuable thing of the value of fifty dollars ($50.00) or less by means of
any false or bogus check or by any other written or printed or engraved
instrument or spurious coin. The term "false or bogus check" shall include
checks or orders given for money or property which are not honored on account
of insufficient funds of the maker to pay same, as against the maker or drawer
thereof. The making, drawing, issuing or delivering of a check, draft or order,
payment of which is refused by the drawee, shall be prima facie evidence of
intent to defraud and the knowledge of insufficient funds in or credit with,
such bank or other depository. Such maker or drawer shall not have paid the
drawee the amount due thereon, together with the protest fees, and the check or
order shall be presented for payment within thirty (30) days after same is
delivered and accepted.
(1987 Code)
10-420: SWINDLING UNLAWFUL:
   It is unlawful to get money or property from any other person or persons or
businesses under false pretenses, deception, cheating or by any other
fraudulent act.
(1987 Code)
CHAPTER 5
OFFENSES AGAINST PERSONS
SECTION:
10-501: Assault and battery prohibited.
10-501: ASSAULT AND BATTERY PROHIBITED.
   A.   An assault is any intentional, wilful, or unlawful attempt or offer
with force or violence to do a corporal hurt to another.
   B.   A battery is any intentional, wilful or unlawful use of force or
violence upon the person of another, or by making any physical contact with
another without consent.
   C.   It is unlawful to commit an assault or an assault and battery within
the jurisdiction of the town. Any person committing an assault or an assault
and battery within the jurisdiction of the town, shall be guilty of an offense.
CHAPTER 6
OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC AUTHORITY
10-601: Resisting an officer.
10-602: Refusing or failing to assist an officer.
10-603: Assault or battery upon police or other law officer.
10-604: Rescuing prisoners.
10-605: Escape of prisoners.
10-606: Impersonating an officer or employee.
10-607: False alarms.
10-608: False representation to an officer.
10-609: Removal of barricades.
10-610: Resisting public officials.
10-601: RESISTING AN OFFICER.
   A.   It is unlawful to resist, oppose or assault, or in any way interfere
with a police officer or any person duly authorized to act as such, while the
officer or person is discharging or attempting to discharge his official duties
within the limits of the town.
   B.   It is unlawful for any person to warn or signal another so as to assist
such other person to flee, escape or evade an officer seeking to make an arrest
or for any person to bar or lock any door or barrier in the face of or in front
of an approaching officer.
   C.   Resisting an officer is the intentional opposition or resistance to, or
obstruction of, an individual acting in his official capacity, and authorized
by law to make a lawful arrest or seizure of property, or to serve any lawful
process or court order, when the offender knows or has reason to know that the
person arresting, seizing property, or serving process is acting in his
official capacity.
   D.   The words "obstruction of" shall, in addition to their common meaning,
include;
      1.   Flight by one sought to be arrested before the arresting officer can
restrain him and after notice is given that he is under arrest;
      2.   Any violence toward or any resistance or opposition to the arresting
officer after the arrested party is actually placed under arrest and before he
is under arrest; or
      3.   Refusal by the arrested party to give his name and make his identity
known to the arresting officer.
10-602: REFUSING OR FAILING TO ASSIST AN OFFICER.
   A.   An officer of the town making or about to make an arrest, or executing
or about to execute a warrant or other process, in accordance with the
ordinances of the town or with state or federal law, or suppressing or about to
suppress a riot, affray or unlawful assembly, may call upon person or persons
to assist him in making such arrest, executing such process or suppressing such
riot, affray or unlawful assembly.
   B.   It is unlawful for any person lawfully called upon thus to assist an
officer of the town to refuse or fail to do so.
10-603: ASSAULT OR BATTERY UPON POLICE OR OTHER LAW OFFICER.
   It is unlawful for any person to knowingly commit any assault, battery or
assault and battery upon the person of a police officer or other officer of the
law while in the performance of his duties.
10-604: RESCUING PRISONERS.
   It is unlawful for any person, in any illegal manner, to set at liberty,
rescue or attempt to set at liberty, any prisoner or prisoners, from any
officer or employee of the town having legal custody of the same or from the
town jail or other place of confinement by the town, or to assist such prisoner
in any manner to escape from such prison or custody either before or after
conviction, including escape from a vehicle of confinement.
10-605: ESCAPE OF PRISONERS.
   It is unlawful for any person confined in the town jail or other place of
confinement by the town, or working upon the streets or other public places of
the town in pursuance of any judgement, or otherwise held in legal custody by
authority of the town, to escape or attempt to escape from any such jail,
prison or custody.
10-606: IMPERSONATING AN OFFICER OR EMPLOYEE.
   It is unlawful for any person to impersonate any officer or employee of the
town, falsely represent himself to be an officer or employee of the town, or
exercise or attempt to exercise any of the duties, functions or powers of an
officer or employee of the town without being duly authorized to do so.
10-607: FALSE ALARMS.
   It is unlawful for any person to turn in a false alarm of any nature or in
any manner to deceive or attempt to deceive the fire department or police
department or any officer or employee thereof with reference to any fire alarm
or reported fire, accident or other emergency or knowingly to cause the fire
department or police department or its officers or employees to make a useless
run.
10-608: FALSE REPRESENTATION TO AN OFFICER.
   It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation, or any agent or employee
thereof, knowingly to make any material misrepresentation to any officer,
employee or agency of the town government in any official application to, or
official dealing or negotiation with, such officer or agency; or to commit
perjury before any tribunal or officer of the town.
10-609: REMOVAL OF BARRICADES.
   It is unlawful for any person except by proper authority to remove any
barricade or obstruction placed by authority of the town to keep traffic off
any pavement, street, curb, sidewalk or other area.
10-610: RESISTING PUBLIC OFFICIALS.
   It is unlawful for any person knowingly or wilfully to:
      1.   Resist, oppose or obstruct the chief of police, any other police
officer, the municipal judge, or any other officer or employee of the town in
the discharge of his official duties;
      2.   Threaten or otherwise intimidate or attempt to intimidate any such
officer or employee from the discharge of his official duties; or
      3.   Assault or beat, or revile, abuse, be disrespectful to, use abusive
or indecent language toward or about, any such officer or employee while such
officer or employee is in the discharge of his official duties.
CHAPTER 7
PENALTIES
SECTION:
10-701: General penalties.
10-701: GENERAL PENALTIES.
   Any violation of the provisions of this part is punishable as provided in
Section
1-108 of this code.
CHAPTER 8
ROAD AND HIGHWAY OBSTRUCTIONS
SECTION:
10-801: Amend 69 Oklahoma Statutes, 2001, Section 1213
10-801: AMEND 69 OKLAHOMA STATUTES, 2001, SECTION 1213:
   69 Oklahoma Statutes, 2001, section 1213 is amended to read as follows:
   Section 1213. (a)   Any person or persons who shall willfully or knowingly
obstruct or damage any public road or highway by obstructing the side or cross
drain or ditches thereof, or by turning water upon such road or highway or
right-of-way, or by throwing or depositing brush, trees, stumps, logs, or any
refuse or debris whatsoever in the road or highway, or on the sides or in the
ditches thereof, or by fencing across or upon the right-of-way of the same, or
by planting any hedge within the line established for such road or highway, or
by changing the location thereof, or shall obstruct said road, highway or
drains in any other manner whatsoever,
   except for gating of certain roadways as permitted by section 12-803 of this
code; however, any preexisting roadway dedicated for highway use shall not be
gated or obstructed in any way, or, except as provided in subsection (b) of
this section, any person or persons who shall willfully or knowingly deface,
damage, destroy or remove any traffic-control device, road sign, signboard,
guide sign or signpost shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor.
   (b)   If any person or persons willfully or knowingly defaces, damages,
destroys or removes any traffic control device, road sign, signboard, guide
sign or signpost and such action results in personal injury to or death of any
person, the person or persons responsible for such action shall be guilty of a
felony punishable by imprisonment in the custody of the department of
corrections for not more than two (2) years, or by a fine of not more than one
thousand dollars ($1,000.00), or by both such fine and imprisonment. Notice of
this provision shall be placed in the manual provided by the department of
public safety which manual is issued for purpose of passing driving privilege.
   (c) The governing body who finds any road or highway obstructed as above
specified shall notify the person violating the provisions of this section,
verbally or in writing, to remove such obstruction forthwith, and if such
person does not remove the obstruction within ten (10) days after notified, he
shall pay the sum of five dollars ($5.00) for each and every day after the
tenth day such obstruction is maintained or permitted to remain, such fine to
be recovered by suit brought by the governing body in any court of competent
jurisdiction.
(Ord. 82, 12-19-2016)
PART 11
PARKS, RECREATION AND CEMETERY
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
11-101: Board of trustees to make rules for recreational facilities
11-102: Fees to be determined.
11-103: Penalty.
11-101: BOARD OF TRUSTEES TO MAKE RULES FOR RECREATIONAL FACILITIES;
   The board of trustees shall promulgate, invoke, create, amend and enforce
such rules, regulations, and other requirements as it deems necessary or
expedient in connection with the use of all recreational and park facilities
owned or operated by the town.
11-102: FEES TO BE DETERMINED.
   The town shall provide by rules, from time to time, the fees charged for any
such park or recreational privileges on any property or facility for
recreational purposes owned or operated by the town.
11-103: PENALTY.
   It is unlawful for any person to use any of the park or recreational
facilities without having complied with the rules and regulations promulgated
by the board of trustees in connection therewith. Anyone violating any of the
rules and regulations, or failing to comply with such, shall be guilty of an
offense, and on conviction thereof, shall be punished as provided in Section 1-
1 OS of this code.

(Reserved)

PLANNING, ZONING AND DEVELOPMENT
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING COMMISSION

CHAPTER 2
GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
12-201: Citation

12-203: Nature And Application Of Zoning
12-204: Regulation Of Use

12-206: Interpretation Of Words And Terms
12-207: Future Zoning Classifications
12-201: CITATION:
   This part, pursuant to authority granted by the Legislature of the State of
Oklahoma in 11 Oklahoma Statutes, article XLIII, sections 43-101 through 43-
109, and article XLIV, sections 44-101, 44-102, and 44-104 through 44-110,
shall be known as the ZONING ORDINANCE OF THE TOWN OF DICKSON and may be cited
as such.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-202: PURPOSE:
   The regulations contained herein are necessary to encourage the most
appropriate uses of land; to maintain and stabilize the value of property; to
reduce fire hazards and improve public safety and safeguard the public health;
to decrease traffic congestion and its accompanying hazards; to prevent undue
concentration of population; and to create a comprehensive and stable pattern
of land uses upon which to plan for transportation, water supply, sewerage,
schools, parks, public utilities, and other facilities. In interpreting and
applying the provisions of this part, they shall be held to the minimum
requirements for the promotion of the public health, safety, comfort,
convenience, and general welfare.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-203: NATURE AND APPLICATION OF ZONING:
   This part classifies and regulates the lands, buildings, and structures
within the Town limits of the Town of Dickson, State of Oklahoma, as
hereinafter set forth. The regulations contained herein are necessary to
promote the health, safety, convenience, and welfare of the inhabitants by
dividing the Town into zones and regulating therein the use of the land and the
use and size of buildings, the size of yards and open spaces, density of
population and location of buildings.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-204: REGULATION OF USE:
   Except as hereinafter otherwise provided, no land shall be used and no
building, structure, or improvement shall be made, erected, constructed, moved,
altered, enlarged, or rebuilt which is designed, arranged, or intended to be
used or maintained for any purpose or in any manner except in accordance with
the requirements established in the district in which such lands, buildings,
structure, or improvements are located, and in accordance with the provisions
contained relating to any or all districts.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-205: ZONING DISTRICTS; ZONING MAP:
   The Town of Dickson is hereby divided into zones as shown on a certain
zoning map, dated January 4, 2010, which is filed with the Town Clerk. The
official zoning map, as amended and all explanatory materials thereto are
hereby made a part of this part by reference.
   Zoning districts in Dickson shall be designated as follows:
Agricultural:
 A-1 General Agricultural
Residential:
 R-1 Single-Family District
 R-2 Multiple-Family District
 RMH-1 Mobile Home Park
Commercial:
 C-1 Neighborhood Stores, Small Businesses
 C-2 Shopping Centers, Large Stores
 C-3 Commercial Highway and Commercial Recreation District
Manufacturing and industrial:
 M-1 Manufacturing, Industrial, Fabricating and Assembling
Public and religious property:
 P-1 Public and Religious Property (Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
 
   The above districts may be modified, changed, or altered to provide for
growth of the Town when deemed necessary by the Dickson Board of Trustees.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010; amd. Ord. 87, 6-26-2017)
12-206: INTERPRETATION OF WORDS AND TERMS:
   Unless otherwise specifically stipulated or required, the definitions of the
words and phrases as used in the interpretation and construction of this part
shall be the most commonly accepted in similar types of zoning ordinances as
used in local areas or the common accepted terms and definition in the English
language.
   For the purpose of these regulations, the words used in the present tense
shall include the future tense; words in the singular number shall include the
plural and words in plural number include the singular, except where the
natural construction of the writing indicates otherwise. The word "shall" is
mandatory and not directory.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-207: FUTURE ZONING CLASSIFICATIONS:
   The current Dickson zoning map reflects nine (9) classifications. Four (4)
of these classifications are reserved for future use in planning of the
community at a later date. Only the classifications shown in section 12-205 of
this chapter will be used at the time of effective date of passage hereof.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
CHAPTER 3
ZONING DISTRICTS
SECTION:
12-301: A-1 General Agricultural District
12-302: R-1 Single-Family District
12-303: R-2 Multiple-Family District

Houses
12-305: C-1 Neighborhood Stores, Small Businesses District
12-306: C-2 Shopping Centers, Large Stores District
12-307: C-3 Commercial Highway And Commercial Recreation District
12-308: M-1 Manufacturing, Industrial, Fabricating And Assembling District
12-309: P-1 Public And Religious Property District
12-301: A-1 GENERAL AGRICULTURAL DISTRICT:
   This zoning district is intended to provide an area primarily for
agricultural endeavors, such as farming, growing crops or raising cattle on
property of five (5) or more acres, or the extraction of various products such
as oil, gas, minerals, rock, sand or gravel from the land.
   The rural nature and low density of population in this district requires a
minimum of a fifty foot (50') setback of buildings from edge of streets, roads,
or highways. It is therefore the purpose of this district to encourage and
protect such uses from urbanization until such are warranted and the
appropriate change in district classification is made.
   Property and buildings in an A-1 general agricultural district may be used
for the following purposes:
      All agricultural land uses, including buildings, barns, sheds or other
farm buildings.
      Freestanding mobile home.
      Planting and harvesting crops.
      Raising farm animals.
      Single-family residence.
   The drilling for oil, natural gas, extraction of sand, gravels, or minerals
and transportation may be permitted, provided the energy operation is conducted
in accordance with provisions of municipal and state laws, including all
statutes and/or regulations involving environmental quality.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-302: R-1 SINGLE-FAMILY DISTRICT:
   A.   Description And Uses: This is the most restrictive residential
district. The principal use of the land in an R-1 zoning district is for
single-family dwellings and related uses. The objective is to provide basic
elements of a balanced and attractive residential area. The total area of any
land in this zoning district shall be less than five (5) acres. This area is
intended to be defined and protected from encroachment of uses not performing a
function appropriate to a residential environment. Internal stability,
attractiveness, order, and efficiency are encouraged by providing adequate
light, air, and open spaces for any dwelling or residence in the district.
   The property and any building for an R-1 single-family district in Dickson,
Oklahoma, shall only be used for the following purposes:
      Detached one-family dwelling with accessory buildings, including a
private garage.
      General purpose farms and gardens. The raising of livestock for private
consumption or show purposes and the training of horses for profit or pleasure
shall be allowed. This usage shall provide no objectionable odors or nuisance,
which offend or adversely affect the quality of life of neighbors and persons
in the district.
      Mobile home must be compatible with other residential improvements to the
neighborhood as to both value and external appearance. Any mobile home placed
in an R-1 district must abide by section
5-104 of this code.
   B.   Area Regulations: All buildings in this zoning district shall be set
back from the street or right of way lines to comply with the following yard
requirements:
      1.   The minimum depth of the front yard shall be fifty feet (50') from
the front of a residence house to the street line.
      2.   The side yard for a one-story residence shall be not less than
fifteen feet (15') on one side and the sum total of both sides shall be thirty
feet (30') or more from the house to a property line.
      3.   Accessory buildings, garages or unattached buildings when located
more than eighty feet (80') from a front lot line may be located not less than
five feet (5') from any property line.
      4.   If more than twenty five percent (25%) of all improved buildings
between two (2) intersections of street have an average setback line of more
than fifty feet (50'), then no building shall be erected closer than the
minimum setback as established by the existing building.
      5.   A dwelling or accessory building located on a corner lot or street
shall be a minimum of fifteen feet (15') from the side street.
      6.   There shall be not less than twenty feet (20') or twenty percent
(20%) of the depth of the lot, whichever is smaller for the purpose of a rear
yard.
      7.   The lot width shall be a minimum of eighty five feet (85') at the
front building line and such lot shall abut a street for a distance of more
than thirty five feet (35').
      8.   A one-family dwelling shall be located on a lot area of not less
than five thousand (5,000) square feet. Where a lot has less area than these
requirements and all of the boundary lines of that lot touch lands under other
ownership on the effective date of these regulations, then that particular lot
may be used for described uses permitted by this section.
      9.   No dwelling or building shall exceed three (3) stories from ground
level.
      10.   The coverage from the main and accessory buildings shall not cover
more than thirty percent (30%) of the lot area on interior lots, and not more
than thirty five percent (35%) of the lot area on corner lots.
      11.   The lot area shall always be of sufficient size to provide off
street parking for two (2) automobiles.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-303: R-2 MULTIPLE-FAMILY DISTRICT:
   A.   Description And Uses: This residential district is established to
provide both low and moderate population density to permit multiple-family
dwellings, apartments, and townhouses. The density and yard spaces shall be
arranged to provide general compatibility with the uses as found in R-1 single-
family districts. Therefore, this classification may reasonably be placed in
locations that are adjacent to the single-family areas or may be used as a
transitional zone. The intent is to further discourage any uses in this
district which would generate excessive traffic or create congestion on
neighborhood streets other than the normal traffic that serves the residents in
the area. (Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
   The property and buildings for an R-2 multiple-family district shall only be
used for the following purposes:
      Any uses as permitted in the R-1 single-family district.
      Rooming house or boarding house (but not motels, hotels or mobile homes).
      Townhouse or apartments not to exceed eight (8) units per building and
duplex not to exceed a two-unit dwelling.
      Two-family dwellings or garage apartment.
      Accessory buildings and uses customarily incidental to the above uses
when located on the same lot. (Ord. 76, 1-4-2010; amd. Ord. 81, 1-27-2014)
   B.   Area Regulations: The area regulations for R-2 multiple-family district
are the same as R-1 single-family regulations, except the minimum size of any
lot in this district shall be forty three thousand five hundred sixty feet
(43,560') and when a garage apartment is located with a single-family dwelling
on the same lot, the area shall be a minimum of forty three thousand eight
hundred sixty feet (43,860') and the sum of both side yards shall be not less
than thirty feet (30').
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-304: RMH-1 MOBILE HOME PARK; MANUFACTURED HOMES, MOBILE HOMES AND TRAILER
HOUSES:
   A.   Mobile Home And Manufactured Home Parks:
      1.   Existing property under twenty (20) acres which has three (3) or
more mobile homes will be grandfathered in (which will not require moving any
homes to comply with this section at date approved).
      2.   Property grandfathered in under this section must follow current
town ordinances prior to the addition or replacement of existing mobile homes
in the future.
      3.   The construction, installation, or creation of a mobile home park or
manufactured home park shall not be less than twenty (20) acres and will
require rezoning of property. It is the intention of the town of Dickson that a
mobile home park or manufactured home park shall accommodate primarily
permanent occupants.
      4.   The applicant must provide documentation of the proposed park by how
it will be platted, streets designated, and a plan for installation of
utilities must be established before the board would consider a public hearing
for rezoning of property. Mobile homes within a mobile home park shall not be
placed on lots or spaces smaller than 2.5 acres per dwelling unit, regardless
of whether or not a charge is made for such accommodations. Residents of a
manufactured/mobile home park do not usually own the land whereon their
dwelling unit is sited; they may or may not own the dwelling unit. All
currently existing mobile home parks located within the town of Dickson are
included in the definition.
      5.   Mobile homes, trailer houses or manufactured homes set in the town
of Dickson including a mobile home park must comply with part 5, "Building
Regulations And Codes", of this code.
      6.   Mobile homes and manufactured homes designated for residential usage
within a manufactured/mobile home park located in the town limits of Dickson,
Oklahoma, may not be used for any commercial or business purpose.
      7.   It is hereby declared unlawful, and an offense against the
ordinances of the town to place, locate, or park more than one mobile home, on
a temporary or permanent basis, on a residential lot or lots in the corporate
limits of the town if said residential lot or lots have metes and boundary
descriptions of fifty feet by one hundred forty feet (50' x 140') or less. This
prohibition shall not apply to recreational vehicles, vacation or camping
trailers, which are placed for a temporary period not to exceed thirty (30)
days, same being motorized vehicles utilized for camping, traveling, and
recreational purposes of renting or leasing pads or lots within a mobile home
park for the purpose of placing multiple units of mobile homes.
      8.   The above prohibition shall specifically apply to a mobile home,
trailer house or manufactured home, which are hereby defined as permanent
housing structures, capable of being moved or transported on a public roadway
or highway, and which are designed for permanent habitation by human beings as
a residence or place of abode:
         a.   Manufactured Home: A dwelling unit constructed to be towed on its
own chassis and capable of connection to utilities for year round occupancy
fabricated on or after 1976, in an off site manufacturing facility for
installation or assembly at the building site as a permanent structure with
transport features removed, bearing a seal certifying that it is built in
compliance with the national manufactured housing construction and safety
standards act, 42 USC section 5401 et seq.
         b.   Mobile Home: A structure of vehicular design, designed or
manufactured for human occupancy, built on a chassis, designed to be moved from
one site to another, and to be used with or without a permanent foundation,
whether or not the wheels have been attached thereto or removed, and which was
built prior to the enacting of the national manufactured housing construction
and safety standards act, 42 USC section 5401 et seq., or before 1976.
      9.   Any mobile home park shall be compatible with other residential
improvements in the neighborhood as to both value and exterior appearances. The
property and buildings for an RMH-1 mobile home park shall only be used for the
following purposes:
         A freestanding manufactured/mobile home.
         Accessory buildings and uses customarily incidental to the above use
when located on same lot.
   B.   Area Regulations:
      1.   All mobile homes, trailer houses or manufactured homes placed or
located in Dickson, Oklahoma, shall be serviced for utility services by the
town, if available, and if not available, sanitation services, trash pick up,
electricity, natural gas, and any other utility service which is ordinarily
used to provide habitable dwellings.
      2.   It is further declared unlawful for any owner, lessee, renter, or
occupant of a mobile home, trailer house or manufactured house to secure or
receive any municipal services, including water, trash removal, sewer service,
electrical power, or natural gas supplies, from any source other than the town,
or an alternative source approved by the citizens of Dickson or by the town
council, including, but not limited to, any device, apparatus or method whereby
an owner, lessee, renter, or occupant of a mobile home secures water,
electrical power, natural gas energy, or any other utility from a neighbor or
residence on an adjoining property or location.
      3.   There will be a business permit of one hundred dollars ($100.00) to
be paid to the town of Dickson. This fee shall be deemed "mobile home park
permit fee".
(Ord. 81, 1-27-2014)
12-305: C-1 NEIGHBORHOOD STORES, SMALL BUSINESSES DISTRICT:
   A.   Description And Uses: This commercial C-1 district is intended for a
unified grouping of one or more buildings of general retail shops, stores, or
service centers for personal services for the regular needs and convenience of
the people residing in the adjacent residential neighborhoods. The convenience
center should be developed as a unit with adequate off street parking.
   The property and building in the C-1 commercial, neighborhood stores, and
small businesses district may be used for the following purposes:
      Any use permitted in the R-1 single-family residential district
classifications.
      Retail stores and shops, which supply the regular and customary needs of
residents of the neighborhood and which are primarily for the public's
convenience such as grocery stores; meat markets; gas stations; garages for
repair of motor vehicles or machinery; dairy products or ice cream stores;
pharmacies; barbershops; beauty shops; childcare centers; dry goods stores;
newspaper, magazine and book stores; small restaurants seating less than one
hundred (100) customers; drive-in restaurants; and other similar types of
stores.
      Small convenience stores containing no less than five thousand (5,000)
square feet in building area.
      Accessory building and uses customarily incidental to above uses.
   B.   Area Regulations: The following requirements shall apply to C-
1 commercial neighborhood stores and small businesses district:
      1.   The front yard of all buildings in this district shall be set back
at least twenty five feet (25') from the street or right of way line of the
front building.
      2.   Side yards on the sides of lots adjoining a residential district
shall not be less than fifteen feet (15') to the particular lot or property
line.
      3.   Whenever the rear lot adjoins a residential district, a rear yard
shall be provided of not less than twenty feet (20') in area.
      4.   When any commercial building is to be serviced or supplied from the
rear of the building, there shall be an alleyway of not less than thirty feet
(30') in width provided.
      5.   The business shall provide adequate off street parking to
accommodate customers with sufficient spaces.
      6.   All driveways used for ingress and egress shall be at least twenty
feet (20') wide and preferably twenty five feet (25') wide.
      7.   For each structure there shall be a lot area of not less than five
thousand (5,000) square feet. Where a lot has an area less than these
requirements and all of the boundary lines of that lot touch lands under other
ownership on the effective date of these regulations, then that lot or parcel
of land may be used for the uses permitted by this section.
      8.   No building shall exceed three (3) stories in height from ground
level unless specifically approved by the Board of Trustees of the Town.
      9.   Multiple commercial buildings may be built with a common wall
located along with property lines of adjacent property within the district.
This wall shall be referred to as a "party wall" and no side yard will be
required between buildings with a party wall.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-306: C-2 SHOPPING CENTERS, LARGE STORES DISTRICT:
   A.   Description And Uses: This classification is established for principal
use of land offering accommodations, supplies, or services for certain
specialized uses such as large community shopping centers, large restaurants
seating more than one hundred (100) customers, motels, hotels, and the general
retail trade, with buildings containing more than five thousand (5,000) square
feet in area.
   Property and buildings in a C-2 Shopping Center, or Large Stores District
may be used for the following purposes:
      Any use permitted in the R-1 Single-Family Residential District
classification.
      Convenience stores, retail stores and shops less than one roof of a
building containing more than a total of five thousand (5,000) square feet.
      Shopping centers, multiple or combination stores such as department
stores, gas stations, motels, hotels, grocery stores, garages for repair of
auto-truck or machinery, professional offices, and large restaurants or drive-
ins seating more than one hundred (100) customers.
      Accessory buildings and uses customarily incidental to above uses.
   B.   Area Regulations: The area regulations and requirements for C-
2 Shopping Centers and Large Stores District are essentially the same
requirements as stated under C-1 Commercial, Neighborhood Stores, except that
if a yard on the side of a lot in this district adjoins a residential district,
then any building constructed on that lot shall be located more than twenty
five feet (25') from the property line.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-307: C-3 COMMERCIAL HIGHWAY AND COMMERCIAL RECREATION DISTRICT:
   A.   Description And Uses: This district is one of the most restrictive of
the commercial districts and is intended to be defined and protected from the
other districts and to provide a wide variety of uses not found in the other
districts.
      Because of the possible objectionable influences that may be created in
this district, it is necessary that the district be located carefully in
relation to other districts in the Town. Moreover, Commercial Highway and
Recreation District shall also provide such features as screening buffer zones
or setback strips between this district and other districts in the
Municipality.
      As the Town and community of Dickson grows, the need for a C-
3 classification will likely increase. When additional land is needed for the
C-3 classification, additional areas may be obtained from other classifications
or by rezoning. (Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
   Since this district is a very restrictive classification, any future growth
or changes must be made by the Dickson Board of Adjustments and/or the Dickson
Board of Trustees by ordinance, addressing special treatment and approaches for
each parcel of land based upon the guidelines as given below. This ordinance
must be enacted before any construction or work is performed on the project.
   A plan or sketch drawn to scale must be accompanied with any application for
administrative review and approval under this section. The plan or sketch shall
reflect proposed improvements and use of any building to be constructed
thereon. Further, parking areas and the location of all homes, businesses and
boundaries of the zoning district within three hundred feet (300') (C-1 small
business), one thousand five hundred feet (1,500') (C-3 kennel), one thousand
feet (1,000') (C-3 body piercing and tattoo) of boundary property lines from
all sides of proposed use of the property shall be clearly shown. The plan or
sketch shall reflect the names and addresses of all property owners or persons
in possession of real properties within the required feet area, and shall
clearly indicate the type of building, plumbing, water, sewer, and streets to
be constructed and the proposed uses of the property. "Property owners" in said
context shall include owners of real property, which adjoins or is contiguous
to the lands to be affected by the plan. Environmental issues shall be
addressed, including appropriate precautions to be taken to prevent excessive
sounds, noise, or odors to the adjoining landowners, before the Dickson Board
of Trustees will give any consideration.
   Prior to any consideration being given to any applicant under this section,
the Dickson Board of Trustees, must first satisfy themselves that adequate
written notice has been given to all persons within the three hundred foot
(300') area described in the preceding paragraph of any hearing or public
meeting wherein the plan and/or sketch, and the proposed use of the property
affected, shall be considered.
   The property and buildings for a C-3 Commercial Highway and Commercial
Recreation District shall only be used for the purposes described in the
subsequent paragraph after the Dickson Board of Trustees have studied each
location as to environmental concerns, including, but not limited to, noise,
odors, sounds, and effects of the proposed improvements and location with
reference to homes, agricultural lands, or businesses adjoining the proposed
location. Furthermore, the planned use shall be reviewed and that proposed use
and any potential use in the future shall receive the express approval of the
Dickson Board of Trustees and any other agency of State or local government
having jurisdiction thereof. In approving any plan or sketch, the Dickson Board
of Trustees of the Town may attach reasonable, specific restrictions or
conditions on approval, which are designed to protect the public health and
welfare. (Ord. 76, 1-4-2010; amd. Ord. 87, 6-26-2017)
   The property and buildings for a C-3 Commercial District shall be used only
for the following purposes or other similar types of businesses:
      Automobile wrecking, junk or salvage yards.
      Body piercing and tattoo parlors.
      Bowling alley.
      Car, motorcycles or horse racing.
      Commercial kennels for cats or dogs.
      Drive-in restaurant or truck stop.
      Drive-in theater or movie theater.
      Feed grinding or sale barns.
      Liquor store, beer sales or tavern.
      Nightclub, dance hall or recreation center, private or public.
      Processing plant, meat or vegetable products.
      Skating rink, roller or ice.
      Small animal hospital or veterinary clinic. (Ord. 76, 1-4-2010; amd. Ord.
78, 9-26-2011)
   B.   Area Regulations:
      1.   A nightclub, restaurant, amusement center, recreation center, or
dance hall seating more than one hundred (100) customers shall be of fireproof
construction with walls of metal or masonry and containing floors of concrete.
The buildings shall be equipped with adequate sprinkler fire protection as
recommended by the National Board Of Fire Underwriters. One lighted exit with
an outside door shall be provided for each one hundred (100) customers or
people. Doors shall be constructed so that they may be opened from the inside
at all times and at no time shall those doors be barred or locked.
      The parking lot of such a structure shall be of sufficient size to
provide at least one parking space for every two (2) customers. The lot shall
be paved with concrete, asphalt or other standard parking lot construction
materials that will provide little dust. (Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
      No building under this section shall be located closer than two hundred
fifty feet (250') from the boundary of any residential district, school, church
or park. One residence or mobile home will be permitted on the property to be
used by the manager or security guard for living purposes only. Any building
located thereon shall be connected to water and sewer. A building and parking
lot under this section shall be enclosed with a six foot (6') high fence on at
least three (3) sides, primarily on the back and both sides for businesses.
Liquor stores, beer sale facilities or taverns shall be located more than fifty
feet (50') from the nearest residential zoning area. The area regulations shall
be the same as given under C-1 classifications. All operations shall be in
accordance with the Oklahoma Statutes and ordinances of the Town of Dickson.
Suitable parking and yard lighting shall be provided. (Ord. 76, 1-4-2010; amd.
Ord. 78, 9-26-2011)
      2.   Meat or vegetable processing plants will be permitted when the
Dickson Board of Trustees approve their locations. The area for such plants
shall be of sufficient size to conduct the business. No offensive or noxious
odor nor loud noises will be permitted in the conduct of said business that
will interfere with agricultural and residence districts. No feedlots will be
permitted. A plant shall be located more than one hundred feet (100') from the
nearest residence or dwelling. The County/State Health Department or Department
of Environmental Quality must approve an adequate sewer system. Sufficient off
street parking shall be provided for plant employees and customers. The area
regulations as given under C-1 Commercial shall apply unless stated above.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010; amd. Ord. 87, 6-26-2017)
      3.   Skating rinks, bowling alleys, drive-in theaters or movie theaters
shall be located more than one hundred feet (100') from the nearest home or
more than one hundred feet (100') from the boundary of any residential or
agricultural districts.
      4.   Small animal hospitals, veterinary clinic, or dog and cat kennels
shall not be located closer than one hundred feet (100') from the nearest home
or boundary of residential or agricultural districts. The area requirements as
stated under C-1 Commercial shall apply, except as noted above.
      5.   Automobile, motorcycle, or horse racing will be permitted if a
suitable location can be found that will not interfere with the adjoining
agricultural, residential, or commercial districts. Consideration must be given
to the noise, pollution, odor, and traffic. A minimum consideration shall be
that such tracks for racing vehicles or animals shall be located at least one
thousand feet (1,000') from the nearest home. First consideration as to
location of such a facility will be given to the effect on agricultural
operations and residences. The second consideration will be given to business
or commercial usage. The last consideration will be given to recreation.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-308: M-1 MANUFACTURING, INDUSTRIAL, FABRICATING AND ASSEMBLING DISTRICT:
   A.   Description And Uses: The purpose of this district is to accommodate a
wide range of manufacturing, warehousing, wholesale, and other activities. The
M-1 Manufacturing District is intended to reserve the land especially for
industry location and operations on major streets or highways.
   Because of possible objectionable influences that may be created in this
district, it is necessary to locate these types of businesses carefully in
relation to other districts to provide such features as adequate buffer zones
or setback strips. Buffer zones and setback strips between this district make
it desirable that these types of businesses be separated from residential and
commercial districts wherever possible.
   Property and buildings in the M-1 Manufacturing, Industrial, Fabricating and
Assembling District may be used only for manufacturing, fabricating,
assembling, repairing, storing, cleaning, servicing, or testing the following
goods or materials:
      Apparel, clothing, dairy products, drugs, and pharmaceutical products,
electrical and acoustic products and components, medical laboratory supplies,
equipment and specialties, optical goods, radio, phonograph, television sets,
parts and testing.
      Food products (except fish, sauerkraut, vinegar, and yeast), furniture,
glass products, metal products, and utensils.
      Paper products, including boxes and containers.
      Trailers, tanks, carts, pipe yards, storage, steel, or metal products.
      Wood products, including boxes, containers and building materials.
   B.   Area Regulations:
      1.   All buildings in this district shall be set back from the front
street a minimum of twenty five feet (25'). No building shall be erected closer
than fifty feet (50') from any residential and commercial district.
      2.   Any operation that produces intense glare or heat shall be performed
within a completely enclosed building and exposed sources of light shall be
carefully screened so as not to be detectable beyond the lot lines.
      3.   No toxic or noxious matter, smoke, gas or odor or particulates shall
be emitted that are detectable beyond any boundary line of any district.
      4.   No vibrations, loud noises, or music shall be detectable by a person
beyond the zoning lot line of a business located in this district.
      5.   No activities involving storage, utilization or manufacturing of
materials; on the other hand, products that decompose by detonation will be
permitted. The manufacture of flammable materials that produce explosive vapors
or gases is strictly prohibited.
      6.   Adequate off street parking shall be provided for all workmen, plant
employees, visitors and customers. Driveways used for ingress and egress shall
range from thirty (30) to forty feet (40') in width, exclusive of curb returns.
      7.   The plant, building and grounds of any business located in this
district shall be kept in good repair and painted when needed so as to present
a pleasing and aesthetic appearance at all times.
      8.   A dwelling for use of a plant manager, caretaker or watchman will be
permitted. The plant and any dwelling must have adequate water and sewer
approved by the department of environmental quality of the state of Oklahoma or
any delegated agency or representative thereof.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-309: P-1 PUBLIC AND RELIGIOUS PROPERTY DISTRICT:
   A.   Description And Uses: This classification of property is established as
a district in which the principal use is for the benefit of the general public,
including schools, churches or religious organizations, nonprofit
organizations, and governmental or municipal use such as a municipal town hall
or meeting facility, fire station, public parks or cemetery. Any public
property, including county, state, or federal government is included in this
classification.
   Property and buildings in the P-1 district may be used only for the
following purposes:
      Cemeteries (not including pet cemeteries).
      County, state, or federally owned or leased buildings.
      Elementary and high schools, including playgrounds, athletic, and
extracurricular activities.
      Health clinic or hospital.
      Public parks and playgrounds.
      Religious activities and organizations, including churches and nonprofit
entities.
      School cafeteria or lunchroom.
      The town of Dickson fire stations, town hall, and any other municipal
building, including a senior citizens' facility or structure.
   B.   Area Regulations:
      1.   School buildings shall not be located closer than fifty feet (50')
from any property line of a residential district. They shall have adequate
parking for the students, educators, patrons, and school personnel. The play
area of any school shall be well lighted. The school shall have adequate water
and sewer facilities.
      2.   Parks in the municipality shall be well maintained with proper
facilities for the public such as water and sewer, picnic areas, tables,
swings, slides, tennis courts and playgrounds. Parks shall be well lighted at
night and policed for any criminal activity. No building shall be erected
closer than fifty feet (50') from the property line.
      3.   All public utilities and service uses, including electrical
substations, gas regulators or stations, telephone, water transmission or
metering, distribution equipment and equipment and structures, water reservoirs
or pumping stations or other such uses shall be adequately screened or shielded
from the side, rear or front property lines in such a manner to be attractive
and not be offensive to abutting properties. This regulation shall not apply to
electric, telegraph, or telephone poles for which no permit shall be required
under this part.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
CHAPTER 4
ADDITIONAL DISTRICT PROVISIONS
SECTION:
12-401: Walls, Fences And Hedges
12-402: Yards
12-403: Sight Triangle
12-404: Parking
12-405: Animals
12-406: Agricultural Zoning Districts
12-407: Illumination
12-408: Firearms
12-409: Fireworks
12-401: WALLS, FENCES AND HEDGES:
   Walls, fences, and hedges in a residential district may be permitted in any
required yard or along the edge of any yard, if no fence, wall, or hedge
located in front of a building shall exceed three feet (3') in height, and no
opaque (prohibiting see through) wall or fence shall exceed eight feet (8') in
height.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-402: YARDS:
   Where the dedicated street right of way is less than fifty feet (50'), the
depth of the front yard shall be measured at a starting point twenty five feet
(25') from the center of the street easement.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-403: SIGHT TRIANGLE:
   On any corner lot on which a front and side yard is required, no wall,
fence, sign, structure or any plant growth, which obstructs sight lines at
elevations between two feet (2') and six feet (6') above the crown of the
adjacent roadway shall be allowed. The improvements shall be placed or
maintained within a triangle formed by measuring from the point of intersection
of the front and exterior side lot lines a distance of thirty feet (30') along
said front and side lot lines and connecting the points so established for a
sight triangle on the area of the lot adjacent to the street intersection.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-404: PARKING:
   The land upon which any off street parking lot is located shall be
controlled or owned by the same entity which owns and controls the land on
which the principal use is located.
   The size of a parking space for one vehicle shall consist of a rectangular
area having dimensions of not less than ten feet (10') in width by twenty feet
(20') in length plus adequate area for ingress and egress.
   Whenever two (2) or more uses for parking facilities are located together in
a common building, shopping center, or other building complex, the parking
requirements may be complied with, by providing a permanent common parking
facility, which contains the requisite number of spaces for each use. The total
number of spaces provided shall not be less than the sum of the individual
requirements. Spaces provided for permanent residents of dwellings shall be
clearly designated and separated from spaces provided for employees, patrons,
visitors, customers, and service providers.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-405: ANIMALS:
   Dogs or cats may be kept at any dwelling provided they are kept as pets.
Care and control of such animals shall be exercised as needed by the owner so
as not to annoy any adjoining property owners.
   Any and all animals, including horses, mules, donkeys, ponies, cows, sheep,
goats, hogs, rabbits, chickens, geese, ducks, turkeys, or other mammals or
fowl, if possession is allowed, shall be maintained in a clean and sanitary
condition.
   If any agency, including, but not limited to, the Carter County health
department or on the other hand, department of environmental quality determines
that there is a health hazard and/or a nuisance from any animal, it may make a
complaint before the board of trustees for the violation or to the Dickson
police department. Any persons who have a complaint voiced against them in this
regard shall be entitled to a hearing before the municipal court of Dickson or
the mayor and board of trustees before any adverse actions are taken. Notice of
such hearing shall be in the form of a citation from the Dickson police
department or by a notice from the Dickson town attorney. This provision shall
not abridge or restrict the right of any individual citizen or resident of the
town of Dickson to make a formal complaint under this section to the Dickson
police department.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-406: AGRICULTURAL ZONING DISTRICTS:
   The regulations for agricultural zoning districts in Dickson are intended to
allow low density development in a manner that will require minimal public
improvements and services. They are also intended to preserve the rural
agricultural nature of the area and to require minimal land use regulations.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-407: ILLUMINATION:
   The use of red, green or amber illuminations in connection with any sign
must be so located that it in no way creates a confusion with any official
traffic signal or on the other hand, may be interpreted by any motorist as a
traffic signaling device.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-408: FIREARMS:
   The use of any land or property of any zoning classification within the town
limits of Dickson shall not be used in any manner as a firearm, rifle, shotgun
or pistol practice range.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-409: FIREWORKS:
   The use of fireworks in the Dickson town limits must adhere to section
10-303 of this code.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
CHAPTER 5
NONCONFORMING BUILDINGS, STRUCTURES, AND USES
SECTION:
12-501: Intent
12-501: INTENT:
   Within any zoning district in Dickson established by this part or by any
amendments thereto that might later be adopted there exist:
   A.   Lots or parcels;
   B.   Structures;
   C.   Uses of land and structures;
   D.   Characteristics of use;
the board of trustees is aware and hereby determines that many of the above
described properties were existing and therefore lawful before this part was
passed or amended by which should be prohibited, regulated, or restricted in
the future under the terms of this part or by future amendment. It is therefore
the intent of this part to permit these nonconformities to continue until they
are removed or cease to function, but not to encourage their renewal or
survival. It is further the intent of this part that nonconformities shall not
be enlarged upon, expanded, or extended. Furthermore, they shall not be used as
grounds for adding other structures or uses prohibited elsewhere in the same
district.
   Nonconforming uses are declared by this part to be incompatible with
permitted uses in the districts involved. A nonconforming use of a structure, a
nonconforming use of land, or a nonconforming use of a structure and land in
combination shall not be extended or enlarged after passage of this part by
attachment on a building or premises, or by addition of other uses, of a
nature, which would be prohibited generally in the district involved.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
CHAPTER 6
REZONING AMENDMENTS
SECTION:
12-601: General
12-602: Application For Rezoning
12-603: Public Hearing Before The Town Board Of Trustees
12-604: Action By Planning And Zoning Commission (Rep. by Ord. 87, 6-26-2017)
12-605: Action By Town Board Of Trustees
12-606: Classification Of New Additions
12-601: GENERAL:
   This part may be amended by changing the boundaries of districts or by
changing any other provision thereof whenever the public necessity and
convenience and general welfare require such amendment or change.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-602: APPLICATION FOR REZONING:
   A.   An application for zoning amendment may be initiated by the Board of
Trustees or by an application filed by one or more owners of property.
   B.   Each application by a property owner shall be accompanied by a fifty
dollar ($50.00) fee, no part of which shall be returnable to the applicant.
   C.   An application for amendment by a property owner shall be accompanied
by a Purpose for Rezoning, drawings and any data necessary to demonstrate that
the proposed amendment is in general conformance with the Comprehensive Plan.
An accurate legal description and map of the land and existing buildings shall
be submitted with the application. The above information is not required when
the application is filed by the Board of Trustees.
   D.   A public hearing before the Board of Trustees will be set on the day of
the regular meeting of the Board of Trustees at which action is sought. A
publication notice of the hearing date will be published in the "Daily
Ardmoreite" one time. The publication must appear not less than fifteen (15)
days prior to the meeting.
(Ord. 87, 6-26-2017)
12-603: PUBLIC HEARING BEFORE THE TOWN BOARD OF TRUSTEES:
   All rezoning changes of amendments will be heard by the Town Board of
Trustees.
(Ord. 87, 6-26-2017)
12-604: ACTION BY PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION:
(Rep. by Ord. 87, 6-26-2017)
12-605: ACTION BY TOWN BOARD OF TRUSTEES:
   The Town Board of Trustees shall approve or reject the application or may
make changes and establish conditions.
(Ord. 87, 6-26-2017)
12-606: CLASSIFICATION OF NEW ADDITIONS:
   All new additions and annexations of land to the Town of Dickson shall be
classified into A-1 Agricultural classification.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
CHAPTER 7
BOARD OF ADJUSTMENTS
SECTION:
12-701: Established
12-702: Membership
12-703: Procedure
12-704: Appeals To Board
12-705: Powers
12-706: Appeal To District Court
12-707: Vacancy In Office
12-701: ESTABLISHED:
   There is hereby created within and for the town of Dickson, a board of
adjustment with the powers and duties as hereinafter set forth.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-702: MEMBERSHIP:
   The board of adjustment shall be composed of five (5) members, all citizens
of the town of Dickson, each appointed by the mayor with the approval of the
board of trustees for a term of three (3) years; provided, however, that for
the first appointment under the provision of this section, one member shall be
appointed for a term of one year; two (2) members shall be appointed for a term
of three (3) years. All appointments thereafter shall be for a term of three
(3) years.
   No one person shall serve on any two (2) committees of the town. In
addition, no two (2) committee members who are related in the third degree of
consanguinity or less by blood or marriage shall serve on any one committee.
   The board of adjustment shall elect a chairperson from its membership to
serve a term of one year.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-703: PROCEDURE:
   The board of adjustment shall adopt rules in accordance with the provisions
of this chapter and the Oklahoma state statutes. Meetings of the board shall be
held at the call of the chairman and at such other times as the board may
determine. The chairman, or in his absence, the acting chairperson, may
administer oaths and compel the attendance of witnesses. All meetings of the
board of adjustment shall be open to the public. The board shall keep minutes
of its proceedings reflecting the vote of each member upon each question; or if
absent or failing to vote, indicating such fact, and shall further keep records
of its examinations and other official actions, all of which shall be
immediately filed in the office of the town clerk and shall be a public record.
The concurring vote of the majority of the members present of the board shall
be necessary to reverse any order, requirement, decision, or determination of
any Dickson administrative official or officer, or to decide in favor of the
applicant on any matter upon which it is required to pass under such ordinance,
or to effect any variation in such ordinance.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-704: APPEALS TO BOARD:
   Appeals to the board of adjustment may be taken by any person aggrieved by a
decision of any officer or official of the town of Dickson. Any person, firm,
entity or corporation affected by any administrative decision of a Dickson
official based on this zoning ordinance may also appeal that decision to the
board of adjustment. Appeal shall be taken within ten (10) days from the date
of the decision by filing with the town clerk a written notice of appeal
specifying the grounds thereof and shall further deliver a copy of said notice
of appeal to the officer that made the original decision giving rise to the
appeal. The applicant shall, at his or her own expense, provide required
property owners lists prepared by a bonded abstracter to the town clerk at the
time the notice is filed. The town clerk shall forthwith transmit to the board
of adjustment all the papers and documents constituting the record upon which
the appeal was taken. The filing of an appeal stays all proceedings in
furtherance of the action appealed from unless the officer from whom the appeal
is taken certifies to the board of adjustment, after the notice of appeal shall
have been filed with him, that by reason of facts stated in the certificate a
stay would, in his or her opinion, cause imminent peril or damage to life or
property. In such case, proceedings shall not be stayed otherwise than by
restraining order which may be granted by the board of adjustment or by a court
of record on application and notice to the officer from whom the appeal is
taken and on due cause shown. Upon receipt of the documents from the town
clerk, the board of adjustment shall fix a reasonable time for the hearing of
the appeal, giving public notice thereof to the persons shown on the
abstracter's lists described in this section, as well as due notice to the
parties in interest, and shall decide the same within a reasonable time. The
board of adjustment may affirm, reverse, modify, or change any decision by an
officer or official of the town of Dickson. Upon the hearing before the board,
any party may appear in person or by agent or by attorney.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-705: POWERS:
   The board of adjustment shall have the following powers:
   A.   To hear and decide appeals where it is alleged there is an error in any
order, requirement, decision, or determination made by an administrative
official in the interpretation or enforcement of the ordinance.
   B.   Powers relative to variation where, by reason of exceptional
narrowness, shallowness, or shape of a specific piece of property at the time
of the original adoption of this part, or by reason of exceptional
topographical conditions or other extraordinary or exceptional situation or
conditions of a specific piece of property that are not generally prevalent in
the area, the strict application of this part would result in peculiar and
exceptional practical difficulties or undue hardship. In said event, the board
of adjustment is hereby empowered to authorize upon an appeal relating to such
property a variation from such strict application so as to relieve such
difficulties or hardship and may further establish such requirements or
conditions relative to such property as would carry out the purpose and intent
of this part.
   C.   The board of adjustment is hereby empowered to permit the following
exceptions:
      1.   To permit the extension of a district where the boundary line of a
district divides a lot in simple ownership as shown on record.
      2.   To interpret the provisions of the ordinance where the street layout
on the ground varies from the street layout as shown on the map fixing the
several districts, which map is attached to and made a part of this part.
      3.   To grant exceptions to the off street parking requirements set forth
in this part when it is determined that the size and shape of the proposed lot
is such that off street parking provisions could not be complied with, and that
the proposed use with an exception will not create undue traffic congestion in
the adjacent streets.
      4.   To grant exceptions to the side yard requirements for accessory
detached private automobile garages on a lot where a conforming dwelling
existed at the time of passage of this part or any regulations.
      5.   To permit the expansion of a building housing a nonconforming use
which meets the following conditions:
         a.   The expansion shall not adversely affect any property in the area
in which it is located. Furthermore, screening or other conditions may be
attached to the approval of the expansion.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-706: APPEAL TO DISTRICT COURT:
   An appeal from any actions, decision, ruling, judgments, or order of the
Dickson board of adjustment may be taken by any person or persons, jointly or
severally, or any taxpayer, or any officer, department, board or bureau of the
town of Dickson, to the district court of Carter County, Oklahoma, by filing a
written notice of appeal with town clerk of Dickson, the Dickson board of
adjustments and the district court of Carter County within ten (10) days from
the filing of the decision of the board of adjustment, which notice shall
specify the grounds of such appeal and the basis for the relief sought. Upon
filing of the notice of appeal as herein provided, the said board of adjustment
shall forthwith transmit to the court clerk of the county, the original or
certified copy of all papers constituting the record in the case, together with
the order, decision, or ruling of the board. The person filing the appeal shall
be liable for payment of court costs and filing fees assessed by the district
court clerk.
   An appeal to the district court from the board of adjustment stays all
proceedings in furtherance of the action appealed from, unless the chairman of
the board of adjustment from which the appeal is taken, certifies to the
district court clerk, after notice of appeal shall have been filed, that by
reason of facts stated in the certificate a stay in his or her opinion, would
cause imminent peril or damage to life or property. In such case, proceeding
shall not be stayed otherwise than by a restraining order which may be granted
by a judge of the district court of Carter County. In said event, notice to the
mayor of the town of Dickson, the town clerk, and the chairman of board of
adjustment from which the appeal is taken shall be given.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
12-707: VACANCY IN OFFICE:
   In event of an appeal to the board of adjustment as provided herein, and in
event a vacancy or vacancies exist in the board of adjustment of Dickson at the
time the appeal is filed, then and in said event, the mayor of Dickson shall
have the authority to immediately appoint a member or members of the board of
adjustment to hear the particular appeal. Members of the board of adjustment
shall be different persons than members of the board of trustees of the
municipality. In said event, the town clerk shall administer oaths to the newly
appointed board of adjustment to hear the appeal or matter in question or
issue.
(Ord. 76, 1-4-2010)
CHAPTER 8
SEMIPUBLIC COMMUNITY ACT; SUBDIVISIONS
SECTION:
12-801: Definitions
12-802: Semipublic Community Act; Requirements
12-803: Gate Requirements For Semipublic Communities
12-804: Annual Inspection Of Gates
12-805: Incorporating Homeowners' Association With The Secretary Of State
12-801: DEFINITIONS 1
:
DEVELOPER: The person, partnership, corporation, or other legal entity who is
improving and developing a parcel of land within the municipality and who is
legally responsible to the municipality for the construction of improvements
within a subdivision or as a condition of a building permit.
GOVERNING BODY: The acting council or board of a municipality.
HOMEOWNERS' ASSOCIATION: A nonprofit corporation, subject to a contract between
each individual member and the corporation.
MUNICIPALITY: A city or town incorporated pursuant to 11 Oklahoma Statutes
section 2-101 et seq.
NONPEAK HOURS OF TRAFFIC: The times in which demand for use of the residential
streets by nonsubdivision residents is not conventional nor high and shall be
defined as between the hours of one minute after six o'clock (6:01) P.M. and
five fifty nine o'clock (5:59) A.M. every calendar day.
PEAK HOUR OF TRAFFIC: The times in which accessibility is routine in the normal
course of municipal wide residential activity, which includes the service time
of school buses, and shall be defined as between the hours of six o'clock (6:
00) A.M. to six o'clock (6:00) P.M. every calendar day.
PERSON: Any person, firm, partnership, special district, metropolitan district,
or general district, association, corporation, company, or organization of any
kind.
SEMIPUBLIC COMMUNITY: A subdivision containing semipublic roads that meets the
requirements set forth in the semipublic community act.
SEMIPUBLIC ROAD: A road in which full accessibility is without restriction
during peak hours of residential traffic and is dedicated to the municipality.
SUBDIVISION: The division or redivision of land into two (2) or more lots,
tracts, sites or parcels for the purpose of transfer of ownership or for
development, or the dedication or vacation of a public, private or semipublic
right of way or easement.
(Ord. 82, 12-19-2016)
 
Notes
1 1. 11 OS § 43-122.
12-802: SEMIPUBLIC COMMUNITY ACT; REQUIREMENTS 1
:
   A.   All of the roads in the semipublic community shall be paved in
accordance with municipal requirements. Paving material shall be minimum of six
inches (6") in depth and be asphalt or concrete;
   B.   It shall be the responsibility of the developer to see that semipublic
communities shall have no obstruction to ingress and egress during peak traffic
hours;
   C.   The developer shall install all utilities and shall construct streets,
curbs and gutters in accordance with municipal standards and the residential
local and commercial collector specifications of the municipality. All
semipublic streets shall have a curb and gutter. Minimum paving standards shall
be improved to have a minimum eight inches (8") of stabilized road base in all
semipublic communities;
   D.   The developer is responsible to ensure that all semipublic community
roads shall carry a municipal bond for a period of five (5) years. The bond
shall be for one hundred percent (100%) during the first year and fifteen
percent (15%) for each of the remaining four (4) years;
   E.   All streets in a semipublic community shall be accessible to municipal
vehicles at all times, through the use and maintenance of a gating system as
provided and specified in section
12-804 of this chapter;
   F.   All streets in a semipublic community shall be serviced with private
streetlights that shall be installed by the developer at the expense of the
developer. Any maintenance and monthly service fee shall be paid by the
homeowners' association;
   G.   All semipublic communities shall be marked with adequate notice that
each street is a "semipublic street"; and
   H.   All amenities shall be implemented and maintained through private
means.
(Ord. 82, 12-19-2016)
 
Notes
1 1. 11 OS § 43-110 et seq.
12-803: GATE REQUIREMENTS FOR SEMIPUBLIC COMMUNITIES 1
:
   A.   Gates for semipublic communities shall be located a sufficient distance
from a main arterial street to allow three (3) cars to line up at the gate
without interfering with vehicles utilizing the arterial street; however, in no
case shall the gate be located closer than seventy feet (70') from the curb or
edge of pavement of the arterial street;
   B.   A turnaround lane shall be provided for vehicles immediately in front
of the access gates with a minimum thirty eight foot (38') radius;
   C.   Speed bumps, road spikes, barbs or other tire damaging devices shall
not be allowed;
   D.   Any adopted municipal standards for streets, sidewalks, fire lanes,
fire hydrants and other engineering and development requirements shall apply to
semipublic communities;
   E.   Any entry keypad shall be located on a pedestal near the normal access
route. The entry code shall be given to the fire department, police department
and all other emergency services of the municipality;
   F.   An emergency activation key or knox box key shall be located on the
keypad pedestal. When activated, the activation key or knox box key will cause
the gate to open and stay open until reset by the fire department, police
department or other emergency services provider;
   G.   An emergency release hitch pin shall be installed on the control arm
from the gate and allow the gate to swing open freely with manual intervention;
   H.   A battery backup system shall be provided for each gate. The batteries
shall be trickle charged to maintain electrical energy, and in the event of
loss of normal electric current, cause the gate to open and stay open until
reset by a responsible member of the homeowners' association;
   I.   The location of all entrance pedestal, emergency activation keys or
knox box keys, keypads, hitch pins, related equipment, operation of gate,
signage, opening design, swinging or sliding operation of the gate, or any
other design specifications shall be constructed and installed in accordance
with the plans approved by the community development director and the fire
chief of the municipality;
   J.   Should any problem occur in the operation of the gate, or any violation
of this section occur, the gate shall remain open and accessible until the
problem is resolved or the gate is repaired and tested; and
   K.   When a covered entry is requested, the minimum height shall be no less
than sixteen feet (16').
   L.   A homeowners' association shall be established by the semipublic
community. The homeowners' association shall be responsible for the following:
      1.   Providing the homeowners' names, addresses and emergency contact
numbers of all officers to the fire department and the police department;
      2.   Maintenance, testing and repairs of all functions of the gate;
      3.   Establishing the access code to the gate and assuring that the Fire
Department, Police Department and any other emergency services have the proper
code number. Changing the code shall not be permitted without proper
notification to the appropriate Municipal offices;
      4.   Accompanying and assisting the Fire Department during annual
inspection and testing of the operating systems;
      5.   Requiring that the minimum gate opening width, including clearance
for all improvements related to the gate, shall not be less than twenty six
feet (26') for a single gate or fifteen feet (15') for each half of a double
gate, or a minimum of twenty feet (20') for each single gate on an entrance
that has two (2) separate lanes for ingress and egress.
(Ord. 82, 12-19-2016)
 
Notes
1 2. 11 OS § 43-124.
12-804: ANNUAL INSPECTION OF GATES 1
:
   A.   The City Manager, upon recommendation of the Community Development
Director, as may be appointed by the Governing Body, and the Fire Chief and
Police Chief, shall approve an access agreement with the developer, homeowners'
association, or other responsible property owners, providing for an annual
inspection of each gate to ensure that each gate is tested to meet all of the
requirements of this section prior to it being approved for operation and
continued operation. The access agreement shall include a hold harmless clause,
wherein the developer, homeowners' association or other responsible property
owners agree to hold the Town harmless in the event that the emergency devices
on the gate fail, and the Fire Department or Police Department are compelled to
crash the gates in order to respond to an emergency call or situation. In the
event that damage to any Municipally owned vehicle is caused by the failure of
the developer, homeowners' association or other responsible property owners to
notify in a timely fashion the Fire Department and Police Department of a new
access code, or failure to submit a key to a new lock on the emergency
activation key, the developer, homeowners' association or responsible property
owners shall be liable for the cost of repairs to Municipally owned equipment
as a result of a crash of the gate.
   B.   Verification of the access agreement and a copy thereof shall be kept
on file at the Fire Department and the Police Department, along with the name
of the gate contractor, address, twenty four (24) hour telephone numbers, and
the developer, homeowners' association representative, or the name of the
responsible property owner, address and emergency access telephone numbers.
These verifications and copy requirements are minimum requirements for approval
of the annual inspection of the gate. The Fire Department shall conduct the
annual inspection on the anniversary date each year of the date of approval of
the access agreement.
(Ord. 82, 12-19-2016)
 
Notes
1 1. 11 OS § 43-125.
12-805: INCORPORATING HOMEOWNERS' ASSOCIATION WITH THE SECRETARY OF STATE 1
:
   A.   Upon completion of the responsibilities by the developer cited in the
Semipublic Community Act, the developer shall ensure the formation of the
homeowners' association by incorporating the association with the Secretary of
State. Upon receipt of the certificate of incorporation, all responsibilities
of the developer shall transfer to the homeowners' association.
   B.   All streets in a semipublic community shall be dedicated to the
Municipality in which the community is situated. All water, sanitary sewer, and
storm sewer systems in semipublic community shall be dedicated to the
Municipality. (Ord. 82, 12-19-2016)
   C.   Detail plans for a semipublic community shall be surveyed and drawn and
submitted to the Municipal Governing Body for their approval or disapproval.
(Ord. 82, 12-19-2016; amd. Ord. 87, 6-26-2017)
